Since the hairs are in a way that you perform three cauteries, or four, in alignment with the length of the thigh, according to the shape of the cautery fire that we described previously; and do not press your hand on the entire cautery, and let the patient be aware on their back; and another method of cautery is that you heat the cautery which has two nerves, as we have demonstrated in the dislocation of the shoulder; and raise the heart which is located near the thigh, or where the blood vessels of the patient come from the left side, and let the elevations that you raise the heart according to the heart, according to the length of the body, and the cautery be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After that, you inflame the two nerves as much as the heart is perceived from the other side, and then you remove the fire from the cautery, and thus there will be four. And if you see, if you cauterize the entire cautery at three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment when he has obtained purity by long tension, and this is better than the other treatments mentioned beforehand.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cautery does not apply to hydropsy, except in the manner that is called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat according to the methods that we have stated in divisions, and your treatment does not profit at all, then it is necessary that you make four cauteries around the bowels, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the spleen, and two behind the back on the spine, and one on the piss; and let the cauteries be well close to the skin of the body.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After letting the cautery open for a short time, and not leaving the treatment of the patient's illness after the cautery; and healing will hasten, and the four intentions will be assembled with the aid of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the stomach should be a clavele, which we have previously shown; and that for the back should be olive-shaped, according to what is written here before.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the inflammation of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in one who is hydropsical, and are full of bitter yellow fluid, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the auricular and anular veins; and lift your hand with the cauter without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too much in depth, thus it would be like the citrine sweat, and let the cauteries be according to this form:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit. de la menoison	of the meningitis
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches. de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is named "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you burn the fleshiness which is named "thelul", if you heat the cautery that seems suitable, and then place it all wrapped up on the burned fleshiness; and hold your hand so the cauteries come to the birth of the vein, from which the blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is much of the fleshiness, if you cautery each one as we have said; after the treatment of wounds, it profits until they are healthy; and if you cautery with a great cautery on the skin, it will have more aid.
de plaie mal curee	of a badly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere. Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When a fistula comes, and it is enveloped and casts putrid and corrupt moisture, if you need to prove all of it at once with a subtle probe, and be careful that you know the entire extent of how deep it has gone.

After heating the cautery that seems to be a rasp, and insert it into the fistula according to the quantity that the probe has entered, and restart the cautery as long as the putrid and corrupt flesh is burned, once, or twice, or three times, according to the quantity of one's need; and beware of injuring the nerves that are nearby, and the large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and to the intestine, beware of these limbs, and do not make false passages in the charned limb, and think that it is not pierced entirely; after healing the limb as much as it may be sound, and if the limbs are healthy, and the materials are removed from afar, then know that the limb is entirely sound; and if the materials are not removed, know that the limb is troubled, and corrupts the bone at the font; and thus one of those things that we will say in its limb.
de la maladie des reins	of the kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide. de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then you should apply cautery to the upper part of the bladder, where the hairs of the pubic area begin, and one on the right and one on the left, and each cautery should be as long as our finger; and make three cauteries above the back, or two if you have need; and the clavicle cautery should be according to the form mentioned before.
de la marris	of the marrow
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit. de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moisture descends to the hip joint, and for this reason it moves out of its place, and the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measuring them together; and it is found that the places of departure are visible, then it is necessary to cautery the patient on the hip joint with one cautery resembling a circle, and mark before the place around the hip as it turns, so that the hip is within the circle; and let the cauteries be such as those with which we have cautered the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauteries are not presented to you, make three cauteries of olive oil, and let the cauteries be as profound as all the veins; and heal until they are healthy.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain in the ankle
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the ankle joint, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is treated for what we have said in the division, but the treatment does not work, and the disease is old: then it is necessary that you purge the patient of gross humors with fetid pills, or other good similar pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After the fire cautery; and the manner of fire cautery is in two ways: it is to know that it assembles burning medicines, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is in many ways, of which one is such: that you cauterize on the surface of the thigh three triangular cauteries according to this form, and it makes good depth and size, and has between each cautery the thickness of a finger, and so are the olive-shaped cauteries; no time is a cautery made in the middle on top of the thigh, because there are four according to this form.
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, if the cautery is made in a circle that we have mentioned before in the dislocation of the thigh; but make it in such a way that the circles encompass the entire thigh, and all the spaces of the skin are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And it is the manner in which one makes on the thigh, when the pain holds in the thigh, and does not reach just to the knee nor just to the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it reaches to the knee and leg, he makes two cauteries there where the patient says the pain holds, and one cautery above the ankle four fingers, a little to the left; and so are the cauteries cutellaire, and so is the thickness of the cord of the heart; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to two toes or near the foot, he cauterizes where he feels the pain three points or four at the cautery which is called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if the masters are, then make more; and if it is known that the pain is beneath the knee towards the thigh, then make a cautery at the shallow or circular cautery, and take good care in all your cauteries that you do not leave so much of the cautery that you burn the nerves and the large arteries, and that you do not cause more great annoyance and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I have seen many who have performed fire cautery on the shin of the foot, and they left it so long that the leg became entirely swollen, and the feet also, and were pierced and corrupted throughout the feet.

Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two adjacent parts, perform fire cautery on one and the other, in this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise men said about the fire cautery of the thigh, that it is in this manner, make the iron thus thick as a small nave of a date, or a little less, and be between the spaces and also from one space to another, the width of a thumb's knuckle; and let the spaces be above two parts, and let them also be like knots, and have a well-made iron handle; and this is the form.
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez. Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use little of this cautery for fear of its regimen, and few see who uses it; and nevertheless this is one of the good cauteries, which can alleviate suffering, and there where it is applied.

And if the pain has extended to the thigh or to the leg, make the instrument that you hold according to what you have done in the same vein previously; and this is the method of warm treatment, and I have written about it in the treatise on medical correction.

Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galien tells us about a treatment where one man was cured of the pain in his hainch and sciatic vein, and he walked much, and said that there is no other treatment, and that he was healthy at once when this treatment was done, and he was bathed as it is instructed hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure. Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And beware that no one should use fire cauterization with such medicines, unless it is after the evacuation of the body.

Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take a woolen thread and the oil of old wine, and put it on the hollow which is between the thumb of the foot and the other called fossile.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	Afterwards take dry goat hair, and burn it in fire until it is charcoal, and put it on the woolen thread, and leave it until it is extinguished; and do it again thus, and cease not from doing thus until you think by sense that it comes to the hip, and that the pain has ceased; and this manner of cauterization is called "goat hair cautery".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from a fall or percussion or by too great an evacuation, or by similar signs of cold matter spread out, none of these signs is worth cauterizing, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary, after this, that the patient is relieved of foul pills or other similar things, that one makes on their back, there where the pain holds, three lines marked with an inch, and in each line 5 or more cauterizations according to the strength and quantity that the patient can suffer; and let the cautery be done according to the cautery which is called "points"; and if you see, make 3 or 4 cauteries at the cautery claw mark, following this form:

After healing the limb so that it is healthy according to what we have said, and beware that you do not misapply fire cautery in a place of nerve spasm.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain in the joints is caused by moisture that spreads to each member of the body, and when pain comes on foot, which the doctor calls "podagre" properly, and when it is from cold cause and treatment with medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in this manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped according to this form.
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary that you prick on the soles of the feet, make fire cautery at every point where they claim "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come just to the knees and other joints, and this happens often, make fire cautery on each knee three or four times on each part, with all the fiery cautery; and if you have mastery of more, do more, but do not hold your hand firm except for as long as the burning of the heart is soothed.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to just above the knee and to the back, administer the cautery that we described in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make points around the finger II lines; and if there remains a point of pain in both, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come to just above the wrists or just above the elbows, cauterize each part, and give good governance to the patient and prepare medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you make good governance for him and you purge bad blood, he will be healthy with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the treatment of the Syphac
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When treatment comes to abscesses, and the boils descend to the intestines and it's new, if it is necessary that when you want to cure the eye, do not touch it with your finger today; and use things that warm the belly, so that the fevers come down from their belly; after make him sit on his back between your hands, and instruct him to hold his arm as long as the boil is repaired, and reset them at your hands, and sign below the treatment on the bone of the finger, and all around a sign that resembles half a circle above the body; then apply the fire cautery in this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until he is pale and until he feels numbness.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the boules to their place; and the ministers hold his hand so they do not return backward; and work well on the thighs of the patient, and put a cushion under him and a servant on the thighs, and another on the foot that holds his hands; then put the cautery on the sign of the entire hand, and the right vein and the left vein as long as you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, so recommence again until you come to the bone; and be subtly warned that the boule does not slip when you perform the cautery; so you do not burn him; and so the patient does not die, or another evil.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And you know that when you do not approach the bone with the cautery, your operations are worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cauteries for children be subtle according to the measure of their bones, and for big people also big according to their measure; after three days cure the bone with a gentle cautery so that the inflammation be removed; after curing other wounds so that they are healthy, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is well healed; and it is necessary that their nourishments be lax for a long time, so that the boils do not burst when they prepare to get up from their beds.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when they want to get up, let them be given a well-made poultice, and for forty more days; and have good rest, so that they work little and beware of too great repletion from drinking and eating, and from too high spirits; and when they follow this instruction, they will be entirely healthy.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will discuss afterwards the treatment of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When wounds come to other parts and are acquainted, and you see that they do not grow anymore, then make the fire cautery in three places according to its quantity, and be careful of the third place of the heart; afterwards treat according to what we have said; and none of the ancients have said that one should cauterize at the cautery at three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the place of the wound and make a line along the width above the wound, and another below, and hold your hand in all the fixed fire cautery.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are more gentle and moderate.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in no member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to a member, either from a fall or a blow, and that pain lasts a long time, and the treatment of medicine is of no value, then it is necessary for it to be cauterized with the cautery called "points", and be careful with the cauteries according to the length of the member and its smallness and weakness and its virtue and location of twisting and of its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If it is well burned by the first cautery, that's good; then name it, and begin another cautery on this one, because such is the custom that it should be changed on the limb that is next to it, so it is necessary that you perform the cauteries until the patient is healthy.
de meselerie	of messiness
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The muscles are often helped many times by cautery with great aid, and similarly the disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	You cannot see that the disease is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not descend or remain, and you doubt that the corruption will not spread throughout the whole disease, then you make five cauteries on the head: one above the forehead, another towards the end of the eyebrows; and two on the horns, and one behind on the nape; and leave it so long that the cauteries reach just to the bone, and until the scabs fall off so that the vapors of the gross humors can exit; and cauterize on the mouse according to what is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the meselry is scattered everywhere; and it appears manifestly, then it is necessary that you apply cauterization to those cauteries that we have mentioned above, and one cauterization on the navel, and two cauterizations on the spine of the neck, and three cauterizations on the spine of the back, and one great one on the chest and another on the sides, and two on the shoulders, and two on the hips, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of the veins that are on the derrière calcant, so you do not burn them; and never apply cauterization to the bone of the finger, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more you do cauterization, the more it helps, and it brings great profit; and know that the patient does not feel any pain from cauterization if they are healthy, because the body is already completely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauterization be large and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the ways of the iron.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	Afterwards, treat the wound with flour paste made with honey and other treatments until it is healthy.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When inflammation occurs in any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and emplasters, but it does not heal, then you should perform cauterization on the member according to its size and smallness of the member; and let the cautery be a little deep into the skin of the body; then treat with ointments until it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And often one performs cautery on the hand and foot and back, at the outlet of the nerve that moves the limb, and thus the inflammation is eliminated; and never does one interfere with it if they are not knowledgeable about the limbs and the outlets of the moving nerves of the body.
de albaras	of the scalps
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is inflamed, and the medicine's engines are worthless, then cauterize with a cautery a little deep, according to the quantity of the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness be removed, and its color be changed; then treat with flour of fenugreek and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of colon and blood of alecost, each one part; and mix everything together, and bind it with a bandage, and apply it to the skin until it be healthy.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of cancer by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When cancer begins to appear, and you want to stop it, if you cauterize at the circle that seems around the tumor, entirely surrounding the tumor.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And always the wise men say that one should perform cautery in the middle of the tumor; and it does not seem good to me, because I fear that it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already wanted to avoid it many times; and a more correct thing is that it should be cauterized around, with the cautery called "circle", as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the inflammation which cannot heal
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When some have an illness called "adubelati", and it delays in healing or because of the excess that it does or because of the age of the patient when they are decrepit (that is to say, very old) and there is little blood, or due to the tension; and you see hastiness in healing: then cauterize extensively with many small cauteries pricking.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it hastens to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see that the entire cautery is pierced, then heat the cautery to the form of which it is:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of that illness called "adubelati" so that the cauteries penetrate to the heart, and let them be such cauteries that the patient feels relief in some manner that the course of the disease is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment so that it may be perfectly healthy.
li cure dou feu par fer	the healing by fire through iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of illness there is which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a withering of the limbs, for it eats away the members just as fire consumes dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in the patient who can suffer from fire cautery, then heat the small and large cauterizing irons according to what is needed for the patient or where the disease is; after cauterizing all parts so that you eradicate all corruption, and nothing remains of it, so that everything that is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let it be for three days, and put on the cauterized limbs a soft poultice with oil until the burns from the fire are removed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of swollen eyes produces scar.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that healthy skin does not grow, it's good; and if not, then restart the cautery on what remains of the corrupted limbs.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this mengeson has often been cured by medicine in addition to fire cautery; but however fire cautery is of greater aid, and I have already said the treatment of medicine in the division: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of pores that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often it happens that our feet suffer from a disease which is called "clos" according to our intention, and it is a big faulty thing that affects the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauterizations of this disease are in two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	It is to know fire cauterization and hot water cauterization.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cauterization is that you heat the cautery iron as if it were a hollow pen, and make it from good strong iron to the measure that it can pierce the nail on all sides, and have subtle margins; then put it totally hot on the nail, and turn your hand totally around the nail until it comes to the bottom of the nail; and leave it thus for three days until it begins to putrefy; then make a plaster of ground savages mixed with oil, and leave the plaster on all night, and the nail will fall out and be disrooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the wound of the joint by anointing it so much that it becomes healthy.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted by defaulters of the body, and many times it happens in the hands and feet, then it is necessary that you apply cautery with warm water; and it is done in this manner: take a cane of iron or a wooden handle, and place it on the nail and the skin, that is to say for removing warts; and place the cane so that it envelops everything around, then put a little warm water, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand while turning so that the edge of the cane reaches the root of the nail, and then you will find the warm water penetrating deeply to the root; and let the patient suffer a little from the burning of the warm water for an hour; then leave it thus, and it will uproot everything to its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Thus you do one after another, as much as you extract those who are in the body, then you treat the swellings that produce flesh.
li cure dou trembler	the cure for trembling hands
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some people tremble from cold or nerves, or from quartan fever or another, if it is necessary that you do three cauteries or four on the spine of the back, one cautery between each spine; and one cautery or foot, and one on the stomach for an olive cautery; thus they will stop trembling, and hasten the health from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of painful pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Never appear by default through the body ulcers, or pus-filled pustules, which come from gross corrupted matters.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	it is necessary first when they appear that one does cautery on each chief of the pustule: a subtle cautery of fire from myrtle, so the point is seized by fire, or root of aristology long, or with lentricular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And never do they cauterize at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow from the inquiry ahead, but are dislodged the superfluous things that come from them, and are healthy; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great outpourings of blood from the artery that is cut in the wound that comes to the surface, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And always when this happens to someone, if you hasten to put your index finger on the wound of the vein, and hold it very still so that the blood is appeased beneath your finger, and does not issue further; then apply fire to the cauteries olive oil more or less small and large as long as they are all red; then take .i., or great or small according to the wound and the place in which the artery is located, and put the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery still so that the blood is stanched.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it happens to flow again when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cauteries are extinguished, then quickly take another of the cauteries that are on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing one thing after another until the blood is stanched; and beware that you do not irritate the nerve which is delicate, and that no other evil does not come to the patient; and know that when the blood flows from the artery, it cannot be well stanched at once because the artery is large, so it is not by one of the three methods that we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strong binding with a thread, or by medicines placed on which have the power to stanch blood; and let it be bound and held firmly in place.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who administers stanching of the blood by tightly binding with strips or putting hard things on, or similar things, does not profit if it does not hold for a little while.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if it happens to no one and there is no better medicine present, then one must put their finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and bind it tightly until it is stanched above the wound and above the vein; and do not move the finger, but keep it still with a cold wet cloth so that it may be very cold until the blood is congealed and thickened and stanched; and make inquiries beforehand about those things which require cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book on surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	Here is the translation:
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the previous cauteries, and for this reason it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I advise you that you do not undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come for a cure.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come of those who worsen so with their illness that they die quickly from the fierceness that they find in their disease, and from the greatness of their evil; and of these one should have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of these there is one who gives his judgment, and says: "wait, I am cured"; and the disease is deceitful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting that you consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but rather place greater caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not open foolishly but wisely of that which you are certain, and of which you can have taken and lost; and use prognosis and indication in the cures of your diseases where salvation may be converted; and this will aid you to acquire good renown, and glory, and long-lasting memory.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, Our Fathers give you good understanding and direction, and if you want to aspire to the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have ordered this chapter by dividing it into chapters, according to what is before or the chapter of cauterizations, that I have devised from head to feet, because you will find more easily what you need to master.
dou chief plein d’aigue	from a head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness comes very often to infants at birth, and when the womb holds the child's head too strongly; and sometimes it happens for a hidden cause that one does not know.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I never saw this disease except in children, and all those that I have seen hasten their death; and for this reason it seems to me that it is worth abandoning the work on some cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose head was full of water, and the head grew so much each day that it could not be supported; and I believed that the moisture was so great that it caused death, and this moisture was assembled beneath the bone under the siphac, between the heart and the bone; and the work is such that the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscesses are small, that you make a large incision in the head; and let it be as long as two fingers, so that the moisture flows; and see here the form of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more abundant, and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and the signs that you see are the commissures of the head swollen on each side, and the water bursts out when you press it with your hand from within, and this does not respond to you: then it is necessary that you make three incisions in the head according to this method:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, extract all the moisture out of it.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After stopping the drainage of tears and powders, and I put in wine and oil, and let it be until the fifth day; then discontinue, and treat the wound with tents and ointments, and let the head dry gradually, and give the patient dried meat without much moisture until the limb is comforted and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you examine whether the opening of the abscess is above, and assemble the water; for it is never in front; never behind; never on the right; and never on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut then where the abscess opens, and fill with water, and do so according to what you have the power to do; and beware that you do not cut an artery; and take care to make a flow of blood, so that the patient may die from the deterioration of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of swelling
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When there is a disease called "catarre" in the eyes or in the breast, and the disease is ancient, and the medical treatment does not help, then the last resort of treatment is cautery with fire that one covers the .ij. arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary then, when you cover the wounds, that the patient makes their head rest; after rubbing the area with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then extracting the patient's neck to the entire cloth; then look where the vein beats, and the veins of one and the other are behind the ears, and are slightly visible; then sign the veins in an angle, then cover one and the other with a sharp instrument of two edges, so that the vein reaches just to the bone, and it should be through the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, insert the pointed instrument beneath the artery and cover it above, cutting similarly as .ij. two at the crossing.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is covered, then the blood flows continuously upward from below.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to feeling, it is necessary that you measure the quantity of the space of three fingers, then sign from the notch and make just to the bone; and it is necessary to put blood flow so it is six cycles, and by chance a little more or less, according to what the patient can suffer, and the replenishment of the artery; then look at the wound: if there remains on the bone point of drainage, if you think that abscesses grow there, then hold the wound and bind it, and the treatment of joints as long as it is healthy.
de emigrainne	of migrating
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient migraine comes, and acute catarrh, because of the moisture of the tears and the cold in the temples and old foolishness and similar things, and it is treated by ways of medical cures and all that does not profit him, if we extract the arteries of the temples and the cauterizations, as we have related.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the way of extracting them is that the patient makes the hairs of their temples grow back, and attends to the artery that opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is hardly restored except in some homes that are too cold; and if it is restored, then the patient strangles with some drapels, then rubs the bone with some rough cloth, and raises the bone with warm water as much as the artery appears manifestly; then takes the spatula of this form.
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then pull it up to the pincers, and separate well the tissues that are beneath each part; and if the artery is subtle, turn it at the point of the uncinate, then take care of that part according to the quantity of the two heads.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For since she is not bandaged, do not touch the wound all over.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	Here is the translation:
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	Here is the translation:
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary to extract the arteries, fill the cavity with a lot of cotton and place well-made tents; and when you remove them, be cured by dry medicines that make the flesh grow, and tents, until it is healthy; and if there is no crust on the artery as long as you operate, if you hasten to cover with cautery, or fill the cavity with vitriol and hold it in your hand so the blood is staunched; and if you do not have this present, place your finger on the cavity until the blood is congealed, and raise the cavity of cold water until the blood ceases, and be steady as necessary; and that which is more moderate and easier in extracting the artery is that you cautery the vein with a trenchant .ij. parts, but the trenchant should be well spaced to wait longer for the heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	Because when the instrument is too tight, it holds less its heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the eyes of the patient, a large space, and then when you have signed on the eyes of the patient, and you hold the burning iron as long as it comes just to the bone, and cover the vein in the eyes; and so are they separated between the eyes because it is not suitable for this cautery from everything to everything; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are descending from the veins that are on the top of the head of fire, and it does not profit from the medicine that one makes, and you see the face of the patient inflaming, and feel a frontal ambulation as if of frenzy; and thus they are tight and moist so that the hairs of the papers are fallen, and the papers are scorched, and burned by the ardor of the tears, so it is necessary to use this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it an "injured cure", and it is that you make a scratch on the patient who has this disease on the hairs of their forehead, then you make three equal incisions on the forehead according to its length; and one of the incisions goes as deep as two fingers into the forehead downwards almost to the nose, and the others go two fingers along the sides of the papers, and beware of the incision of the arteries that are two fingers along the sides of the papers; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the jawbones, and each wound has a quantity of three fingers across the joints; and have prepared a piece of sponge and many strips to suck out the blood, then apply the spatula skillfully in two parts according to its shape.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision that is to be made on the temple up to the second incision; and scrape out all the crust that is between the three wounds to the very skin that is on the bone, then make another part of the mean incision up to the other second, and then extract with this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you put in the first wound the instrument that is called "scalpel", and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is dull, not very sharp, and that is the form;
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting edge towards the airy flesh at the heart, and let the soft part towards the bone, and let it be so until it reaches the middle wound.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes as far as the incision continues until it reaches what opens at the heart, and then make another incision in the middle wound up to the other defect; and then extract the blood evenly, and press the flesh for the taken blood; then put in each wound a tent of old cotton, and put on dressed moilliez with wine and oil and axle, and beware that apostemes do not come; and on the third day, dislodge the lien, and I will minister great plantain water, then cure with ointment of basilicon with rose oil, and other cures which heal wounds, until it is healthy.
dou reume des eulz	Let the hairs grow back.
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When a vein is accustomed to frequent inflammation, and you see the hairs thin and small, and the vision is clouded, and the papers are burned; and the hair falls out, and where the head hurts in front of the pain, and the patient is exhausted; then know through these accidents that those matters and that catharr come not only from many veins, and the treatment is difficult because it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you instruct the patient to shave his forehead, then make a great incision in the forehead, and another as wide as the thumb.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin from the incision of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision be just up to the bone; and separate your hand from the nerves of the temples that move to the brain; and when the bone is uncovered, suck out all the blood with a sponge, and then sew between the two lips of the incision and put in much cotton, and tie with thread; then lay over drapings moistened with wine and oil, and beware of hot abscesses; when it is healed, you must rub the bone so that the flesh begins to grow, then cure with things that make them heal.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take three parties of flour of wheat, and of colocynth three parties, and make a plaster; and apply it to these wounds to expel char throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the swelling of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of these three things: either grains, or beast, or mine stone or similar thing like iron; or seed, like jasmine, beans, peas; or flowing thing like water and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the pierced ear or in some other way that does not join to the ear, nor grows into the ear, put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, distill some drops of violet oil or sesame oil, then prepare for extraction; and when you perform the operation, hold the nostrils steady when the operations begin, and place pieces of cloth or wool over the ear; and hold the ear above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times the fever comes from this treatment; and if it does not come, prepare for extraction with subtle pincers, because that is its form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it gets cured through the pincers, that's good; if not, make an extraction with a subtle instrument of small double hook; and if it doesn't get cured by this, make a cane of iron and push the head of the cane or perforate the ear strongly, and block what is around the cane so that nothing can enter with the cane; then pull out the form, for many times it gets cured as we have said; and if it doesn't get cured in this way, take glue from which one takes the bones, and put some instrument that is pointed for this purpose, and put a bit of cotton around; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it is, and pull out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not sweat from all these things that we have said, then hasten to open the ear thus that an abscess falls out with spasm; and the manner of opening is that you first make the patient's head healthy, and extract blood according to its strength, then place the patient between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear where it depends on fat or flesh; and let the incision be as wide as a moon, until you reach the stone, then scrape with your power, and suck hastily into your mouth; and heal until they are healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot exit, then administer a spatula with a subtle touch according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and prepare an incision of that grain.
