Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do it when you think the grain is moistened by the moisture of the ear, so much that you have made many pieces; then extract with subtle pincers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction may be alleviated.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water, then, that falls into the ear, it is necessary that the patient use the steadiness of condition first, and fill the ear with much cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let it be leaning on that same ear where the needle is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it gets stuck there for that reason, it’s good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If it doesn't, take many piercings according to the length of your thumb and fingers, and heat them a little by fire; and put a patient's ear on one side of his ear, and hold it with another stone on the other side, and make a piercing on the stone which is in the ear; and do not cease from making piercings from stone to stone until the needle is stuck entirely; and if you see, take the joint, and put one of the heads in the ear, and the other head takes fire until the most tender joint is burned; then redo another part of other joints until the needle is stuck entirely, as we have said in the piercing.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is of small body, thus like a thorn and similar thing, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of great body that one can feel, thus amenistrated extraction of pincers; and it is the lightest thing to remove which is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you cure them as we have said in the division and where you treat distillations, and the cure does not profit at all, thus it is necessary that you examine the ear in the sunlight: if you see no worms, take them out with subtle pincers, and if they do not appear, take the vein of what is its form.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be tight below and broad above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And put the most subtle remedy in the ear according to the quantity of the patient's suffering, then suck it forcefully into the vein; do this often until all the veins appear.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey to exit, stop up the vein with cotton as I have said in the stone; and if they do not sweat forth as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have experienced in the treatment of worms, and you will find them or treat with distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all this instrument, from which it is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it is of silver or copper constricted below at a small opening, and expanded above for distilling; and to press down into the distillation with an instrument of well-made copper, and if you see take the scraper and envelop it around the point with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and what you want of your medicines into the vein, and the vein is in the ear; then insert into the scraper all the cotton, and press your hand temporarily until the oil is distilled or comes out of the ear; and the patient feels it inside, and it is the distillations that are slightly warmed by fire, so that they are distilled into the ear; and be careful that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the swelling of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have a hole in their ears; and this same thing happens to men through swelling of the wound, or a boil that forms inside the ear, and these swellings sometimes go deep into the ear, if one cannot see them; and sometimes it happens that the hole becomes small due to the boil, and one sees it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which goes deep inside, if one cannot see it, is of grievous sanitation in many dispositions, and in that which one sees, you must place the ear of the patient in the sun; and look inside: if you see the apparent opilation, if the work has all this spatula-like form from which it is made.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be smooth and flat in front and behind, so that it does not block the ear; if the opilation is from a boil or abscess of the ear, if you take subtle pincers, and gently touch it, so that the boil is entirely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the opilations are deeply rooted in the ear, take a subtle, light razor and heat it slightly over the fire, then place it in the course of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the obstruction where the patient feels great pain in the ear, perceive it lightly, and be careful not to touch the nerves of the ear; then put a tent in the ear according to the width of the perforation, and apply the Egyptian ointment in the junction.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not leave it for a day until the wound is soured, or take a tent and mucus in rose water, and powder with vitriol broth; and if you see the ear inflamed, it is necessary that you remove the tent and replace another mucous tent made of rosed oil and wax, until the inflammation is removed; then cure until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if a flow of blood comes, dip a sponge and wrap it in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other cures that remove the flow of blood which are treating with distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Here is the translation:
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without decay, if the cautery fire subtly burns the lens-like skin, and the cautery expert afterwards makes it worthless; and many times they repair, as nothing remains of their roots; and when they are burned by fire, so are those roots destroyed and do not return.
de la gresle	of the fat
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times there come in papers of the eyes things that seem rough in their shape and hardness, and because of this, this disease is called "grandine", and it is a gathering of gross moisture above and below; the operations are such: take a ward if the grandine moves from one part to another, and it's a light thing to know; make the donkey of large size, then gently scrape each part, then take it with pincers, and cover.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cover it sensibly by piercing a little the paper, do not hurt the patient; and if the fissure is large, assemble it with a suture, and cure until it is healthy; and if it is small, do not use force, for the junctions restore it quickly and without pain.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grandine descends into the depths of the ear towards the upper part, invert the paper, and grasp the grandine with pincers, and cover and press from one part to another; and if the paper is separated by the incision, do not grieve anything; and when the grandine is covered, lift the oil of salt water, and cure the limb of what charity brings as long as the patient is healthy.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Here is the translation:
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press on the limb with your fingers and feel the crackling within.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the treatment is that the patient puts his head in a healthy position; and then takes a thread of linen, and sets up a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains fatness from each part, then places it on him; and presses with your fingers on one side and the other, so that the fatness is gathered within the circle; then makes a slight cut with a sharp scalpel, and does not make it larger than the wound made for bloodletting; and makes the skin deep enough that you reach the fatness; and in many dispositions the fatness comes out of the cut, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Draw out then with a piece of charpit cloth between your fingers at the bottom, and turn your hand to the right and to the left so that it is spread; and be careful not to touch the cut, that you do not reach the whole scalpel just up to the eye, that you do not make it bleed.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the patient does not open at the beginning of the wound, apply a small amount of gentle pressure to the wound so it opens; then hold steady as we have said, then spread a thin layer on the affected area and water, and put it on the limb, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who break it and put it back in place to correct that moisture which has stayed behind.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess comes to the limb, then treat it with soothing ointments until it is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When in papers hairs are born joined to another than the natural ones, and are enveloped, if they harm the eyes, and cause various kinds of diseases such as accustomed tears and softening of the papers and albumin, so that it is the cause of destruction of the eyes; and the cure is according to .iii. ways: either by cautery with fire, or by medicine applied according to whether it is before or chapter of cautery, and is done either by incision and stitching or by cauterization, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the head of the patient in your healthy state, then turn the paper of the eye with your left hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, prick a needle at all points; and let it be beneath the margin of the paper where the hairs grow beneath these hairs, and draw the thread above all the paper, and turn to the ruler; then make in the part beneath the paper, beneath the hairs adjusted, all the spatula coping, from the large needle up to the small; then extract the thread, and place beneath the paper a small piece of cotton and drapery, then sign on the paper an image of an anchor, like the leaf of myrtle, and it is necessary that the image be according to the quantity that you see elevated the paper which is divided into sections.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is a need for a dressing, take a large quantity of paper according to how much the paper is moistened; then spread it all over the spatula along the two lines that you have signed, and start from the great artery up to a small one; and let one of the fissures be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the onion in one of the two angles of the heart, then scrape everything; then assemble the two lips with a suture of a needle and all the subtle thread of linen, and suck out the blood, and make the superfluous filaments on the two eyebrows disappear into nothingness, if you want to do this; and if not, if there is no cure, then leave the suture and threads for three or four days; then treat the wound without a dressing of dry and constricting things, because the paper will revive suddenly from the wound and its assembly, but the dressing is deadly (as the ancients said), and it's work without fear; and if there is another way: and it is that you sign the paper with a figure that should be like the leaf of myrtle, as we have recounted, three onions' worth according to the form that is here.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then apply this which overcomes small equal forces uniformly according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the tongs, and the thing is not equal, take a needle or thread, and put it in the figure; and put another thread through the large artery, and the second thread through the small one, and assemble them evenly between your two fingers; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin on which you have made the sign, as we have recounted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by suture, and cure until it is healthy; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar ointments soothing; but none of the times does the hair of the papyrus convert: so you must use what we have said about the incision; but the suture on one side and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of wounds is according to this form: and it is that you convert the parchment and make it dense according to what I have said, and then make .ij. wounds by art, and .ij. subtle stitches as long as the parchment and the width of the spatula is; and apply as .ij. heads of .ij. parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly above what overcomes the parchment of the eye, and strain the .ij. wounds of the .ij. parties firmly; and leave it thus for some days, and the skin that was strained will become numb and harden, and putrefy, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, if the scalp has forces, then cure until it is healthy; and when the wound is sewn, and if the papyrus is lifted, and they will no longer sprout hairs; and this is the shape of the two canals that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	Here is the translation:
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the pursuit is treated and the hairs do not come with it, so pull the pursuit to the underside along the entire thread that you have ordered it, until the pursuit appears through two pertuses above and you see it by the vision of the eye; then if you pull the pursuit and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for 8 or 9 hours, until the hairs are rooted in their place and the flesh grows over; and if the hairs are short, so accompany them with a long hair from natural whiskers, and be elevated with that which you leave, until it is elongated and then set free.
de la porriture de l’oil	from the vision of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or the putridity comes into the eye, it has two manners: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, or from a cut, or from a cautery, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of the work is that you make a suture, and separate the lips of it, and put in threads of linen, and bind it so it may be healthy; and it does not seem to me that you should use in the cure of it things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do that, the disease will return worse than the first; but it works with softening things, like fenugrec; and the rose water or attar and linseed oil are applied, and ointments of dyaquilon fondut in any of the eyes, and it is wrapped in a cloth, and this is the cure for that.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your cure are that you take heed not to let it sink back into its original form; and these works that we have spoken of are only remedies for this illness, so that it does not relapse into its original form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is beneath, truly named "axacrati", is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and fractures and cauteries and similar things; and the way of working on it is that you take a needle, on which there are two threads, and fix it in the flesh, and make it pierce through the left arm vein as far as the right, so that the threads enter into the head of the flesh; then place the flesh above the entire needle, and cover with a large spatulum.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns according to what is needed, it's good; if not, take a razor and put it in the wound, and turn the paper, and make two wounds or sutures within the paper; and be the heads of the two wounds at the angles of the incision that you have covered, and make one angle so that when they are assembled, the figure is like the figure of a letter which has no "I griesche"; then remove this flesh, according to the quantity whose sides are adjusted below, from what follows the paper, then join the two separated parts, and sew with a thread of linen; then apply the cure of what we have said about mollifying medicines and tents, until it is healthy.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a wound or a break or a cautery, it is necessary that you make a plain wound beneath the hairs of the papers, and according to what is presented before; then remove between the .ij. leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters appear to arrange everything so that they can make it return to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what he needs of treatment and instruments in many dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	because of the suddenness of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this joint has mains homes in such a way that the paper above is soaked with the white of the oil, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then it is necessary to put the point of a razor beneath the paper, and lift it high; and hold as pincers, so that you grasp what is attached to the subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too blunt, so that the patient may not suffer from the too-sharp or too-blunt spatula touching the oil; and make your incision, by carefully scraping off what is assembled, lightly, so that the paper regains its natural shape; and it is all healthy, and never again becomes inflamed with salty water, and raises a gentle and soothing warmth, and of collar; then put between the paper and the oil a linen tent, and place on the oil a soft, abundant ointment; and after three days use gentle collars and soothing things until it is healthy.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the corner of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	You know that the corner is affected in two ways: it is nervous and similar to a hard, rough spot, and another which is not nervous but appears as a white, moist, congealed humor, when touched with iron and pricked with pincers, if it cannot be om; and both and other appearances start from the great eyelid, and increase little by little until it covers all vision and all light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is that the patient puts their head in a healthy position, then opens their eyes; and holds the skin with one hand, then coils the corner with pincers of small double wire, and stretches it upwards; then takes a needle, and inserts a horsehair, or a cow hair, or an ox hair, and a strong thread; and doubles the point of the needle a little and fixes it in the corner, and pierces it all the way through, and holds the corner with a thread and stretches it upwards, and scrapes all the hair from the side of the corner which leads to the prune and the swoop of the hair just at the head, then cuts off the remaining part at the root of the eyelid with a subtle and fine force, and lets the natural flesh or eyelid heal, so that by the incision, the course of the tears does not become accustomed; and never does the corner settle into the onion-shaped wound, nor to the thread, as we have said; then scrapes all the subtle skin from which this form is made.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the skin does not touch the raw flesh and breaks it, and that the prune is not perceived; and after the incision, put a little of soothing boric water in the eye, and make a collar of litargyrum, and leave it until the next day; then cure what he needs so that he may be healthy.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot apply the needle, and the nails cannot enter, many times this type of nail is cured by medicines; and grows as I have recounted in the division, and if you see it covered, so open the eye of the patient, and take the lighter spatula according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And raise the nail subtly, and if you see it diminishes to a point and the reason approaches, so distill from your mouth into the hollow of the colon made of litargire and red colon and broiet, and stop up the eye just until the next day; then recommence the other work according to this same method, until it is entirely restored.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing opposes you in the eye, as if an aposteme is hot, then apply the lathe, and first cure the hot aposteme until it is healthy, then recommence the work as before, until it is healthy.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the arm hurts at night in the eye by great annoyance, so suspend it from the nail, and cut off a part but not entirely, because the flow of tears does not come; then distill into the hollow red colon made of litargire.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh which grows on the fingernail
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Here is the translation:
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But always it is necessary that you elevate the cure of each oil weak from the natural way; and from the accidental way, in work of iron; and do not put your hand in any of these works as long as you see that this member is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	There are red veins that are covered on the eye, and they take away its function and blind the eye entirely for a long time.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary therefore at first that you examine the eye, in which there is a defect, it is strong, and there is no other disease besides this defect; then thus proceeds the treatment: instruct the patient to put their head in a healthy position, then suspend those veins all around according to their wisdom, and let the delicate double onions be according to this form.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two onions by degrees in the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then you coil the strong veins subtly, and extract the blood hour after hour, until you see remove those veins from the eye; and beware that you do not block the eye at the points of the tiny pores, and perform this operation at midday in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your operation so that you do not grasp more than those veins; and when you have done this, then distill in the collyrium green and red to corrupt what is remaining of the vein.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot collect all that in that hour, then make a poultice on the eye of soothing things to alleviate the pain of the eyes, and let it be for some days until the pains are alleviated and are assured of a hot abscess, then recommence according to this manner which is presented beforehand until it is healthy; and this is the form of the treatments:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mirror is named "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with fire cautery and burning medicine according to what I have said beforehand, and it is not yet healthy, if it is engendered in the eyes that you make an incision on the abscess, there where it must be opened, and remove all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.

Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives. se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the eyes are cloudy, and there is birth, and the body of the eyebrow is cloudy, and it remains thus for 40 days, and it does not become inflamed and is not apostematous, and bad accidents do not occur, knowing that it is healthy; if not, if there is no other remedy than to bring back the fistula to the opening of the nostril according to this form: and it is that you discover the bone for the second time with iron, and with bitter medicines, and when it is discovered thus take the forest according to this form, and let the head of iron be at three angles, and let the fistula be attenuated up to the head as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide. de l’issue de l’oil	of the discharge from the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez. dou derrompement de toile uvee	because of the tearing apart of a diseased vein
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions come in the diseased vein, then it opens, and comes forth like grains of resin, and is astonishing to see; then if you see the vein clogged, the operations are such that you put a needle at the root of the affected part below, then put another needle where it has double thread from the affected vein; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to its disposition; then take hold of the vein with double thread and bind one part of the vein around, and hold it well, then pull out the needle and put it on the same moist place in abundance of water; and let it be until the threads join with the vein, then cure the eye with comforting things as long as the wound is healthy; and often the wound is restrained by the vein each part of a circle of cloth, until it is healthy.

And if the eyes show great appearance, then pierce with a subtle spatula which comes in front of the eye, and correct the moist albugeous matter and descend beneath the eyes, and enter soon thereafter; then hold it steady until it is healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the orbit of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing but a bubble that forms in the eye, appearing as a water drop, and it's not really a water drop; and the manner of appearance of the work is that you make the patient sit on a prepared seat and straight, then take the head between your hands from both parts, and move so that you see the bubble come up to your eyes; then be fixed, and do not descend or scatter the light, and see the patient's things as they usually are; and if it does not descend below, know that it's a water drop, and if the descents of the bubble are not apparent as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Here is the translation:
des aigues de l’oil	the veins of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the similarities of wounds in the division, and this is what is necessary to perceive; if one operates according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you sit the patient between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and hold the healthy eye firmly; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eyes are left-handed, or in your right hand if the eyes are right-handed; then take in your right hand, if the eyes are left-handed, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eyes are right-handed; then place the point of the instrument below the crown by the thickness of a thread in that white part of the eye at the least painful spot, then insert the instrument called "almagda" gently, and twist your hand until it penetrates into the white part of the eye, and feel that almagda reaches the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the way of almagda be according to the measure of the spaces which is from the prunele to the end of the blackness; and this is the crown of the eye; if you see the bone in that paper through the clarity of the woven fabric, and then place the instrument near where the wound is, then press it down one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	Here is the translation:
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After rest, the patient rises by the second path, puts the fire with the instrument, and when it is thus fixed and does not rise, then extracts the almond gently turning the hand little by little; and then adds to the ague a little of the gemstone, and relieves the eye within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then puts by default the eyes steeped or washed in rose oil and in abundance of egg white, and binds with the healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our kind, put on common broth with an abundance of egg whites.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the maggots cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have very hard eyelashes, it is necessary that you take the instrument called "alberit", which is thus formed:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And you pierce the conjunctival sore, and do not go too deep in the font, but make the subtle passage, then extract the almond as we have said; and at the completion of the work appearing to the patient who is sleeping, in which he sleeps on his back in the dark place; and be careful of all movements, and take light food, and does not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and be tied according to his disposition until the third day; then untie him in that same dark house, and tests his sight, and makes him see certain things, and then puts back the bandage until the seventh day; and it is not necessary that you do this at the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you delay this, because the ague rises hastily.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	Here is the translation:
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then he leaves the house little by little, and converts into his case; and knows that no disciples should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in his country they made maggots perciet, which drew out the water, but nevertheless I never saw any of them in our land, nor did I ever read about them in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the similarities of the forms of amputation, because those who do not know them go astray; and thus they should be properly prepared.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And thus the head of the bone is in this subtle joint, and the last one in three angled corners.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh above the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	No times are born or born various diverse characters, because there are some that seem like scorptions with many feet; and if it has such a character of fixed color, and if it has a character of soft bone-colored.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case of those characters which are soft and not fixed, you must make the patient sit between your hands against the sun; and open their nostrils, and throw the onion at those characters, and treat them with fires; for you know how to sustain the subtle spatula on one side, as long as you know that this character is all ostensible.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that cannot be cured, open everything .i. of the subtle instruments gently, so that nothing stays; and without overwhelming yourself, or an abscess bursts, drain it as it should; and if they are malignant apostemes, hurry and cauterize until the blood is stanched and all the flesh is burned away, then pour in water or vinegar and wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nostrils do not open, and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healthy; and if moisture does not penetrate as it should, know that there is a character born in the above bone, which the strumens do not come to cut: then you must put the thread of flax a little thick, and be careful with our hands, and have between each nail of space I ought or less; and put the patient's head at the end of the thread in his nose as one can, and treat it odorously until it comes through the nose into the mouth; and many times children do thus as schools, and it is an easy thing for him who wants to do it; then hold the head that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and know one after the other in being as we are with the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do so much that you know how the nodes have corrupted this flesh, then pull out the thread, suck out the blood, and apply the thread in Egyptian stitching, and put it back in place as before; do this for three days or more, until the stitches corrode all that remains of flesh; and then put a compress on the wound for several days until it is healthy, and if there is need of medicines afterward, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, where they distill oils and medicines in the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or copper, resembling a lamp cover, like a small tube, and guide it thus; and if you see, make a small tube close by, and let the instruments be plain for cleansing the head; and have .i. a handle on the head to hold it when one heats the oil or any liquor.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh above the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" occurs on the head above the nose, and it grows and becomes large, so much that it is visible to behold; and therefore you must burn the tumor at its beginning, and remove all the flesh, then apply the cautery or burning medicine; and if you delay in covering until it becomes large, take care if it is hard, of a dark color, of poor sensation: if you do not touch it with iron for it is an encrusted abscess, for when you cover it many times, great evil comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of dark color, and you see that you can completely cover it, then you cure the patient and remove their fear, and heal the place with drying and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is covered and swollen
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when continuous suppurations come into one of these cartilaginous wounds, it profits little, because in some homes.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary then to cancel what has happened to none, if you see that the wound is fresh in all its blood; and then adjust the two lips to a seam, then heal until it is healthy; and if the lips are already separated from one part to another, it is necessary that you scrape all parts of their skin until they heal, then assemble the two lips to a seam, and hold them in place, and sprinkle with powder of dragon's blood, and burn incense; and put on the powders a piece of strong or other suitable plaster, and let it stick by itself, then heal with stitching until it is healthy.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the treatment is that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as we have said in the treatment of the belly wound; or with thread, as I have made you aware.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At the hands of men who have dens abscesses on the lips, similar to grains of vezes, and smaller and larger; then it is necessary that you turn the lips, and divide into each node, and take them as pincers and cut into each part; then apply the lee after the incision of vitriol broth, so that the blood is staunched; and then apply the oil of Hazel, and cure the lip of dry things until it be healthy.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times it is necessary to cauterize the gums that are swollen, which the ancients called "albulus"; if it is necessary for you to hold them in place with bandages, and apply a poultice at their root, and let the blood or wound flow; then put on top of the vitriol ointment, or other powders that constrict and dry; and if this swelling returns after incision, and many times happens, if you cauterize it for the second time, and it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of treatment for coping with excess flesh.
des sordens	of wounds
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are assembled at the top of the teeth, deep in the mouth between the gums, scabs which are smooth and slippery; and sometimes the black, citrine, and greenish teeth come to corruption, and are foul-smelling; if it is necessary for you to hold the patient's head between your hands, and their jaws be in your saint, and take out the teeth or scabs that appear, until nothing remains; and thus do with the blackness and greenness, and jaundice and other stains, until they are cleared; and if one removes what is at the first root, it is good; if not, then start again on the second day and the third, until you have taken everything out; and know that teeth have need of various forms of treatment for removal, according to what the work demonstrates, because the roots that one removes from the teeth have other forms than those that are between the teeth; and these forms and others will be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat a tooth with pain that you delay to handle it as much as you can, because one should not hurry to do it; for it is a very high substance just up to then that one has no excuse to hurry.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained to undergo treatment, it is necessary that you be certain of the tooth's ache.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain deceives the patient, and they think it is in a healthy tooth, and they treat the good tooth; and yet the pain does not depart from them, until the bad one is estranged, for we have already wanted to do this to those healthy ones; and when you are well certain of the aching tooth, then it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth on all sides with a spatula strongly to ward off the gum from all parts; then move your fingers or subtle tenacities at first a little and a little, until they are well estranged, then hold the tenacities firmly; and let the head of the patient be in your healthy hands between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and insert it gently into each part lightly, and remove it as you did at first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is perceived and gnawed, it is necessary that you fill it with drapels, where the perforations are; and if you hold subtly as tongs, so it does not break while holding; and it is necessary to work very skillfully around the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And you do well to beware that you do not break it, and leave a part remaining, and return to the patient by the malice of the root which causes greater pains than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not act like ignorant surgeons, who in their haste and hardness often break the cartilage, and do not amend what we have related; but they come to it through the obscurity of this great malady caused by the roots that remain, or by the cartilage that breaks, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is drawn, if you wash the place with wine or vinegar and salt; and if a discharge of blood comes, which often happens, if you apply the place with vitriol broth; and if this does not work, then cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	Here is the translation:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be of large limbs so they do not bend in the track, and let them be of well-made iron, and let them be toothed to hold in place.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains in the wound, it is necessary that you put on the wounded place a moist cotton cloth for a day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the wounds are softened, then apply the tongs called "algefri", because the head seems to be in a state of healing; and they should be made thus like a file and that is their shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to issue into all these pincers, then you must uncover the flesh entirely around the root, and put the instrument called "althali", that is to say a scalpel, of which this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and big so it does not break easily, and if the root jumps up through that, it is good; if not, then you aid with all the instruments, from which the forms come afterwards:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one aids with this instrument which has many rules, from which the form is:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are presented in the arrangement of the teeth, and of this instrument which resembles a large clamp, from which the form is:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let these instruments be strong so they cannot break, and know that many of the teeth's instruments are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise masters subtly find their own instrument, according to what their works and the disease demonstrate, for there are some diseases where the ancient ones did not teach at all about an instrument due to the diversity of ages, and it does not break in the cartilage or in other bones, or it pierces, if one searches for the instruments that are needed, which I have told you, and aid with the gestures, from which the form is:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be thick and hold well to hold the bone, so it does not slip away, but can hold and ostrude; and then restore the lever of convenient medicines for that, and if there is porousness in the bone, and it is small, then take all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural body shape, and its form is ugly, especially in small women, then it is necessary that you know if the teeth are not after the tooth, and it is not in the right place, and one cannot smooth or file: then take the file; and if it is sharp with the tooth, then take this instrument which has a similar shape, and is like a small beak, and is of iron inde at the end of the instrument.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the handle is small and small in the hands for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can file it, then file with a part of the file as it is its shape.
