et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file of which one makes the needles; and in filing the tooth small and small in the hands gently, so that it does not move too much while it cuts; then smooth out the end to remove any roughness, and if the teeth are too pointed and they bite the tongue, then it is necessary to file the asperity until it is even, so that it does not bite the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth aches
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front tooth is dislodged, either by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press on it so that it does not slip, and you have treated them with medicines that constrict, but it is of no use; if you need to hold it back with a thread of gold, for the silver thread turns green and rotten, but the gold one never moves; and let the middle thread be neither too large nor too small, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you want to reposition the teeth, take the thread and pass it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the head between the bad teeth, even if there is one or more, until you arrive at the healthy tooth on the other side; then recommence the covering up to the part where you began, and hold your hand subtly and carefully, so that it does not move at all; and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then gather the heads of the thread to a tin, and assemble them, and place them between the healthy tooth, and set it so it does not touch the tongue; and then leave it thus straight as long as it can stay, and if it dislocates, or the threads break, hold it with another thread; if it stays and serves thus all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the adjustment of the two healthy teeth, and the two fingers, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, you put it back in its place, fresh from fresh, as we have said; and do not intervene with one who is not wise and suffers, and never makes the form of a tooth of ivory from a cow, and puts it in the place where the defect is, and holds it in place as we have said, and stays and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	from the copper of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	It never happens that the threads which come from under the tongue or naturally, do not stay thus; or by accident of a wounded palate; and the operations are such that you open the mouth of the patient, and hold his head in your healthy one, and lift the tongue; then gather the nervous thread of large size, so that the tongue is dislocated from its holding, and if there is hardness or numbness, and it is suddenly wounded, if you anoint with unguent and gather the large ligament; and beware that the fissure is not too deep, for the artery which is underneath; and when you have done, lift up the water of rose-water and of vinegar, or of cold water, then put under the tongue a strip of linen; and touch the patient every night, so that the wounds may heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the flow of blood comes, put the vitriol ointment on the spot; and if the wound is vain, then cauterize it with a slow cautery fire, which is good for this; then treat another treatment until it is healthy.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see the color of the wound as copper or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it declines to a blister, and there is moisture, then anoint with unguent, and make a subtle spasm of the skin, and deliver from one part and another; and if the wound does not heal according to your work, then put on vitriol bruised as much as it is stained, then return to your work until you have treated everything fully; then lift up the water of willow and of seed, and cure with other cures until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there come ulcers in the throat called "godath", and they are properly called "II amandres"; when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healthy, beware: if it is a hard abscess with little sensation and dark color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also because of the flow of blood; but let it be until it is ripe, and then you will remove it, or it would break apart by itself; and if it is of a pale color and the root is subtle, adjust the instrument to cover, but first check if the abscess has cooled down and is calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and their head should be in good health, and open their mouth and grasp the instruments between their hands, and press the tongue underneath all the instruments, because this is the form; whether it is of silver or subtle iron, just like a small knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Here is the translation:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, take a candle, because it is the shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be cutting from one part, and name the other; and when you have cut one of the armatures, cut the other in the same manner, and after incision gargle the patient with hot water, and hot and cold, and if the blood flow is stopped, gargle the patient with hot water, or apply poultices of green grapes so they are ripe, or leaves of myrtle, and similar things, until the wound is staunched; then cure until it is healthy; and no other time do abscesses grow in the throat except the two armatures, if you cut them thus like the two armatures together.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was nestled deep in her throat, it is to be known as a small abscess; and it had almost closed off the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the passage which was obstructed, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained thus for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had grown so much that it had almost put out two veins through the two openings of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then, and inserted an onion into one nostril, then the flow was heavy, and a large portion of blood came out; then I made another insertion in the other nostril, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterwards I inserted the onion into these abscesses, and cut away a part, and only a little blood came out; and thus the passage of the woman's throat was unclogged, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not cease to cut away at that abscess for a long time; and the abscess receded again, and refilled the void I had made, so much that it became very large; then I ignited it and cauterized deep in her throat: thus it remained without growing further; and I parted from these parts, and knew only God could do something about it afterwards.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the vein descends to the skin, and it is inflamed and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is thick and rounded, it is called an "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is purified as we have said in the division, and the purification does not benefit at all, and you see that the swollen abscesses are alleviated, and it is subtle; then it is necessary to cut it; and the one that is rounded, gathered, and not long; and it is sanguine or of reddish color or black, then it is necessary to avoid the incision of it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is necessary, therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue against the instrument which we have mentioned before; then prick the vein with a needle, and draw from beneath, and cut around two of the instruments that I have said for the incision of the two handles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the excess flesh which is beyond the natural term; for if you cut more, it will grieve the voice and the speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the II amandres, and cure until it is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear about cutting, it is necessary that you use gentleness at the cautery of the senses for fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of cautery is sharp and pointed.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts his head in your healthy hand, and then presses the tongue to the instrument that we have said or chapter of cautery, and confines with a sharp lively heat, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and in employing the movement of this instrument, from which there is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Here is the translation:
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, not like the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take calament and ysope and origanum and rue and camomille and avronne and similar herbs, and assemble them all or some of them in a pot, and put ash in it, and make it boil; and the pot should be well glazed with strong earth, and in the pot there should be an instrument that filters according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it is of silver or copper, and let one of the heads be placed in the patient's mouth as long as the vapor rises to the eye through the cane, so that the eye becomes mortified; afterwards, you begin frequently, so that the eye dries out, and beware that you do not do this at the beginning of the appearance of a hot abscess, for many things happen; and do not do it further unless at the decline of the hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put a piece of egg white in the chief, so that the patient's mouth does not become too hot; for the egg white does not let the vapor pass into the mouth, and it is a good remedy altogether, safe.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it happens at the throat or spine of a fish, or something else; so you must treat what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you can see the thing clearly; and what does not appear and is stuck in the throat, you must make the patient vomit so that the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps by chance the thing will come out through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of turnip, or a root of lettuce, or a crumb of dry bread; and attach the sponge to the thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, it will be stuck, and then pull it out further; and if it does not come out from what we have said, take the instrument for extracting according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the curved instrument be at the head so that it can enter more lightly into the throat, and hold the head high lifted; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest everything goes awry, nor does it push inside; and it is of value that the patient holds the instrument, because it is held or the thing is easy; if it holds below, where it draws everything equally along the entire instrument, as long as it goes smoothly.
de la sansue de la gorge	from the sensitivity of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	No medicine is suitable for the wound, as I have said in the division, through the treatment of medicines; and when this does not profit, then look into the patient's throat towards the sun, then press the tongue to the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the vein, pull it out completely with small forceps, or subtle tongs that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if it's not suitable, take a curved hook, and insert it into the patient's throat, then make a movement with the hook to draw out the iron that is hot.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if you tease the patient with water all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full view of cold water, and open the mouth, and let it glide in sensibly, and move it with his own hand often; and if you feel the vein sense the water, then bleed.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it doesn't bleed as we have said, then suffumigate the patient with acetite, with the instrument that I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will fall without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the method of fumigation is that you take a pot where there are visible coals, and it is placed covertly in a perforated container, and in this container the head of the instrument; then you throw in the fumigation, and the patient puts the end of the cane into his mouth, and closes the mouth, so that the smoke does not escape, but reaches just to the wound; and the wound will now heal, and if it does not heal, then recommence the fumigation many times; and the patient suffers thirst, and eats salty and bitter things, and does not drink any water; and then the treatment is complete when it is expelled through this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument to which one treats the blood, if it is, when one can see it, similar to bent tenailles entering the throat; and it has the appearance of a beak of a sign, and it has roughness of lime, so that what it takes, it cannot let go; and see there the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the surgeons of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many abscesses are similar, according to what is remembered and comes afterwards in this book, and they are diverse in perforation and in size; and it is in two manners, one of which is in its own resemblance, and because it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is for the cases where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the body are different from those that come in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses that should not be pierced, as long as the bowel is mature according to its accomplishment; and if there are such that it is necessary to pierce when they are ripe, and do not die according to their accomplishment, like abscesses that are on the joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come from the joints, and one lets them be until they are ripe within, perhaps because the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is in the principal member, and you delay the perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the principal member; or if it is in the foundation, one should pierce it in this way so that it is ripe; and it is not necessary to pierce a ripe abscess without complete digestion, except for that which is in the foundation, lest it putrefy within, and become fistulous, and cannot be healed in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the sign of perforation of the abscess which is ripe according to its accomplishment, and it is when the pain is appeased, and the departure from fever, and the diminution of pain and redness, and gentle debate and arrangement of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it is necessary that you make sit the perforation or more depending on the abscess, and where it appears most; and let the perforation be long in the course of the body, and if the abscesses are in hands or feet, or joints and veins, and in all equal parts where there is no putridity.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, one should apply a cautery to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the flesh, it is better that you let the perforation until it is confirmed by complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it in front of that, the clean body of the venom will flow from him, and it is full of much filth; and by chance they will harden the lips and the deep parts of him.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there are any abscesses that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limbs have need of.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you make small openings for small abscesses, small perforations; and in large abscesses, large perforations, and many incisions according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to shave the skin, and cover; when it has become thus as I dress, and is softened, it is necessary to do thus as one does for blisters: and if there are those that are cut in three angles, and if there are those that are covered like the leaf of myrtle, as abscesses of the groin; and if there are those where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Here is the translation:
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the desperate patient has often succumbed to the issue of the bowel, which by chance kills the patient, and you do not perceive it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid, then, this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, if you evacuate the wound, and examine whether the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a plain ulcer, if you apply tinctures of flax or cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, then you must put a tent over each so they do not touch one another; and if you have cut into the abscess a part of the skin, and you have shaved around, then you must fill with much cotton or rasping of flax thread in the sense of moisture, and place it just to the third day; then remove it, and cure by ointment until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if you remove blood that has come to the surface of your work, if you handle it with cold and dryness, and wrap it in a cloth, and place it on the limb that is suffering from repeated removal.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the blood removal persists, you should handle it with governance and cure, and the powders that I have mentioned in my book, and if it is winter, and the limbs or abscesses are very nervous, then you must put on warm and oiled tents and drapplings; and if it is summer, and the limbs are hot, then you should put on cool and oiled drapplings, or in wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then dislodge the abscess and the swelling and the cure, as it is fitting, until they are healthy.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to understand universally in the treatment of abscesses: for you have said how one must proceed before treating abscesses, and see here this chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where wounds occur from small abscesses, and there are ways for us that are in veils, just like the swelling of a gland, and much is similar.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There is fat and such things where there is moisture, just like pus; and if there are such things that are hard and piercing to the cutter, and there is no doubt that the artery does not act contrary.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the operations of the cutting are such that you experience everything with the instrument called "entromissoire", from which the form comes after this, whatever it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then they make a passage downwards along the length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is evacuated, then they scrape without leaving any skin that contains this moisture, for it returns immediately when one leaves nothing; then they plunge cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, with water and silk, and they fill the wound, and leave it until the next day; and they correct what has remained of the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then reapply the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain painful at night; then treat the wound of piercing in a suitable way, so that it heals.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds in a fatty substance, then cut according to this form, from the length; and you will throw out the uncines, and scrape off all parts, and put all your treatment of drawing forth for the cotte where it lies; and if the artery makes you do the opposite, then do what I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And thus do with the abscess if it is porous, and of cutting and of curing as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut into the porous abscess and the moist one, if it is lighter, for they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if there are any of these abscesses or heads where there is no moisture, and among these I treated the head of an old woman; and found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and bluish, and could not break it open; and if one had made a strong effort, one would have done harm like breaking into a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming on the head, those which come on the heads of children and at the roots of the ears, one should open them so that they are completely dependent on the patient, in order to issue forth the pus; and the treatment should be as it is necessary.
des scrophules	of the scalp ulcers
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur on the neck, and beneath the shoulder blades, and in the groin area, and sometimes they come from another part of the body, and are numerous, and are connected with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each ulcer is properly located within its side, as the swelling and abscess of the head, as we have said; and the similarities of these ulcers are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that case where you see a good disposition in the touching, and it is similar to the color of the body, and moves from one part to another without being airy as nerves to the collar or to the artery, and it is not deep; so it is necessary that you cut above, and scrape off each part, and remove the two lips of the heart as onions, if you are in mastery, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and pull gently, and be sure that you do not touch the nerve or the vein, and do not let the spatula slide, lest your hand slips, and do not push too far, so you do not touch what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut into the vein or artery, and it does not let you operate, then put on the wound a vitriol ointment, or some powders that staunch blood, and hold the wound steady; and let it be until the abscess is appeased, and the wound becomes soft, and begins to heal.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is staunched, return to your work, until you complete it; then inquire with your finger whether there remain any small scrophulae, if you cut and mend them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrophula, it does not behoove that you cut into that scrophula at its root, but rather tie it with a strong double thread, and let it fall away by itself, without harm; then fill the wound with much cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out the entire scrofula, it is necessary that you assemble the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, then there will be no more excess flesh due to the greatness of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you understand to cut at the root of it, and make a groove, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofula that have excess flesh, pierce where it appears to die; and pierce thus as stated before, depending on the condition, then treat with ointment and similar things, so that it does not corrupt what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, treat with ointment, heating the char, until it be healthy.
de squinance	of squinting
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old ones said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I never saw in our land who did it, and it's the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinting, it is necessary that the partition of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be examined; and one should not do anything except by this, because all the veins and the pormon of the patient are at those who have an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in the mandrels.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the pormon, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary, therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it beneath three circles or four small cuts across, between the two circles or by the quantity of the cut which passes through the syphac, not in the cartilage; and thus it is convenient for the section of the epiglottis that there be no char, and the vessels are long enough to inquire.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the masters are fearful, then it is necessary that they stretch the skin of the throat to the entire neck, then cut through the heart as far as it reaches the canal; and let out the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then touch the syphac, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the flux of the canal which goes forth through the broken limb, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed in which one doubts the strangulation, assemble the two lips of the wound with a sweet cure, and sew underneath the sense without the cartilage; then administer medicines that make flesh grow, so that it may be healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Do not stop doing this just so long as the throat is completely stopped up, and the patient is judged to be near death, and lacks breath.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then touch the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and they inhale through the wound, and thus are protected from death; and therefore the old man commands to leave the wound open as long as the evil of the disease has passed, and it will have passed in three days or four. And then he commands to sew up the wound and cure, until it is cured; and I shall tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a maiden held the cautery, and thrust it into her throat, and burned part of the sinews behind the arm; and I was called upon to cure her, and found her almost dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and I found the blood that was issuing from it, and I knew well that it had not been properly covered with a bandage or dressing other than the throat, and the veins were pouring out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened, and sewed up the wound, and cured her until she was healthy; and it did not take long for the maiden to regain her voice, and afterwards returned to her usual disposition; because I saw that in the tailoring of the epiglottis there was no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "throat hernia", and it is a great abscess in the color of a jaundice, and it is very common in women; and it has two manners: natural, and accidental; or naturally there is no obstacle.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental is in two manners, of which one is similar to a fatty tumor, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from a blockage of the artery; and there is fear, and it does not need to open the false fluxes except in the one that is small, and you try and search throughout the entire interior: if you find it as I do not see a fat tumor, and it does not penetrate at any vein, if you cut, if you cut like we cut the tumors, and you draw out all its coif, if there is none; and search very thoroughly, and cure it as it needs, until it is perfectly healthy.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways of ours, which I will describe all the similarities; and now it is necessary that I explain all the differences that exist between us and them.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that the patient is feverish and has a chill, as long as the inflammation has passed, and it has accomplished the putrefaction; then the fever and chill are restored.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the patient having no heat nor fever nor pain, and containing yellow bile, which is their own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins as a jaundice, and becomes thick; and are according to the same similarities, whether grey, or moist, and many colors are so as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the ninth node, that you examine and inquire first about all the instruments which are called "entromissoire", according to its form whether it comes from a chapter or a treatise which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inspecting the abscesses in us is that you take or more moist heat than you find in the abscess, and turn your two fingers little by little, until you feel that the instruments have pierced the heart, then according to the size of the abscess; then extract the intervening matter, and take care not to cause harm.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	Here is the translation:
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if he remains still, the pain returns to him many times; and if it stays for a short time, and without grieving the wound, apply powders of corrosive water, and hold the wound steady, and put on soothing aposteme ointments hot, and treat other treatments until he is healthy; and if the pain is great, cut the lips of the wound, and treat what injures within.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein is swollen against you, or otherwise, hasten and apply the vitriol ointment, and leave it there for 8 or 10 hours, until the wound suppurates, and restore the ebullition of blood; then return to the copper that which has been removed from the navel.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of inserted instruments, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are four squares that are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and there are three ways: large, medium, and small, to encircle the apostemes of fistula; and they are also like the needles whose tips are cut, and are of citrin iron, or silver, or copper, and those that are yellow are more experienced for piercing the fistula wounds; and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the wounds.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of onions are very similar, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and if there are onions that have two curvatures in three ways thus; and if there are onions that have three curvatures, and are thus of three ways; and if there are onions that have two curvatures, and onions with a single curvature only, and are of three ways; and all this is necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these instruments is sharp, and there are those that do not cut except from one part, which peels the nails, because one does not touch the vein or nerve; and these inserted instruments are the lancets placed in handles, so that the patient does not feel it at the opening of abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and we do not use them except on charnut flesh, such as legs, arms, and limbs, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling a fistula scraper, according to this form, to staunch blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and one puts it sometimes at the healthy spot that connects the veins, and the arteries, and sometimes one finds according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Here is the translation:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Here is the translation:
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the sitting (or perhaps "of the seated" or "of the sediment")
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the sitting are kinds of hard scrofulous tumors which have ribs, and there is only moisture that they contain.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture must be treated according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is evacuated, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with ointment coming to that point so it becomes healthy.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are similar to scrofula, do it as we have said in cases of scrofula, and if the wound is full of pus, apply fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	from the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is broken, and the skin above it is swollen, abscesses often occur, and similarly, the vein becomes inflamed and abscessed; and if you examine it thus, as it is due to the artery, the abscesses are long and profound; and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel the strangeness; and when it is due to the vein, there are obvious signs of fear; and it is foolish to try to cure this abscess, especially when it is under the ribs and in the hollows and near the neck and many other places, and it is very great.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	You must then abandon the treatment with iron, and the one who is at the head of the artery must also abandon it, and in the one who has inflammation of the artery caused by a blow above the skin on the loin; then open the incision as wide as an ounce, and carefully separate the artery from the tissues, so that it may be discovered; then insert a needle beneath it, and make it pierce through to the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then touch the place which is between the two ligatures of an intromissoire, so that the blood may issue from it, and be free from the abscess; then begin the treatment with gentle manipulation, until the ligature holds firm; then treat what is inflamed, until it is healthy; and if the abscess is due to the incision of the vein, you must hold in your hand what you can of the abscess, and insert the needle beneath the place that you hold in your hand, and make it pierce through, and have a double thread, so that you may draw it from the other side; then ligate the abscess, as I have told you, or with a ligature of one of the two parts of the thread at the head of the fillet; and if you doubt that the thread does not hold firm, insert another needle through all the threads beneath the entire abscess to the incision of the first needle, and tie the threads in three places; then treat the abscess until it is free from excess, then treat the excessiveness of the blood and leave what is tied; then put on a dressing made of soft cloth soaked in wine and oil, and apply treatments of tents and ointments until it is healthy.
des apostemes des ners	of the abscesses of the veins
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also, how abscesses come into the artery and into the vein, they come into the veins when they are injured, or by too great exertion, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And it often happens to the joints and the two and in all places where there are joints, and it's the painful abscesses, and their color seems like the color of the body, and it is in many dispositions without pain; and when one strains forcibly, the patient feels pain, and it's not at all in the depth of the body, but beneath the skin; and it moves well from all parts, and does not go forward or backward, nor beneath nor above, and that which is in joints cannot be cured by iron: perhaps it would contract by chance; and he who is in the head or forehead, makes the skin on the spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscesses are small, then hold them with tongs, and cut at their root; and if they are large, then suspend from the groin, and scrape, then bone and assemble the wound to the suture, and care for it until it is healthy.
des grosses boces pendans	the large hanging lips
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Here is the translation:
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I examine them and found in one 18 ounces weighing, and in the other 6 oz., and the work of incision is that you observe if the patient's moisture is humid, and the color of the joint is pale and moist with subtle root; if you apply the spatula large, and be present with fire cautery.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Because when cutting often occurs too great a flow of blood, and if you don't stop it, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the incision with iron, take a well-made thread, and bind the joint as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then restrain it, and do not cease from tightening the thread until it holds the joint, and thus ends the work; and if the roots are thick, fear to cop at the same moment for the belly, but you can well cop half, then cauterize so it does not return; then cure the wound, and beware that you do not touch the tissue that is of faulty color and poor sense and little regard.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an encrusted abscess, and I will come to the treatment of chancre hereafter.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the skin is on fire
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the swelling comes from cautery of a wound or crack in the skin, and it is on the belly and in some of the veins, just as it has happened in other ruptures, or of blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is in front, or of windiness; and if it is by the rupture of the skin and by the issue of the vein, if the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and opens into diverse issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is through the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses with their fingers, it recedes, and then returns, and by chance, it becomes narrower, and grows much at the entrance of the bath, and through strong labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is by moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press with your hand, it does not constrain at all; and if it is by blood, it opens by these signs of large and hard abscesses, and is fixed according to a quantity; and if it is by windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the works are that you look to see if the appearance is by the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It is necessary that you leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in this chapter on abscesses, regarding the artery and the vein.

And if the appearance is in the intestine or the bouillon, then it is necessary that you instruct the patient to hold his arm straight and be fully extended; then sign above the swelling; then instruct him to sit between your hands, then go above the place where you have signed the entire circumference; then tie it with a strong thread or a cord of strong silk firmly, and make sure the vein is well-sealed; then uncover half of the abscess spread above the vein, and put your index finger in, and explore the intestine; if you find the vein taken, then release it, and put the intestine back into its proper place; and if you find the bouillon, then take it to the uncine, and remove the superfluity; and if the artery opposes you, or the vein, then go gently above, then return to your work and take two needles, and put them in the filz, and put the two needles above what you have done in a cross that you make piercing; then extract the abscess from four places above the needles, and if you see it, remove the needles, and let the place heal as long as it can, and separate the dead flesh by itself; or cover it when it is subtle and putrid, then cure what is necessary, and shave the abscess as we have said; and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place of what is necessary, and sew the place.
dou chancre	a chancre disease
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	Here is the translation:

And the operations, when it is in its place or where you can osteer, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile several times; then make him healthier if he has manifest repletion, then anoint the patient with good health to perform the operation; then cut your incisions or tumor, and shave all parts, and remove all excess flesh without leaving anything; and let the blood flow freely, and hold the limb firmly in your hand or in something, and see that the blood does not make a contrary motion against the incision of the artery or vein, if you cauterize so that the blood is stanched; then cure with another cure until he is healthy.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already said in the division the similarities of hydropisy, and how the assembly of the water is done, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: it is clarified simply; and one should not touch with iron in these two similarities: it is to know, tympanites and yposarche, for it is a mortal thing; therefore when you medicate this hydropisy similarity called "clarified" by medicines, and the cure does not profit, if you see the patient is weak, or if they have another disease besides hydropisy, such as pain and solution of stomach and similar things; if you do not touch with iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient is very virtuous, and they have no other disease except hydropisy solely, and it is not too young nor too old, then you must operate: lift the patient straight up in your hands, and the ministers press the stomach in the lowest part of the back, then take the spatula with spine according to this form.
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let there be cutting of two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And let it be a point, and always avoid being so inside that it cannot come near the intestine when you make an incision, and do not let it bleed; then see if the dropsy is inclined towards the intestines: if it needs to be opened on the right side of the intestine III fingers deep; and if it is for liver disease, let the opening be on the left side of the intestine III fingers; and if it is for the spleen, let it be on the right, and do not let the patient lean on the incision so that the superfluous fluids do not flow to the weak spot; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and cut, and lift your hand at all the space between the skin and the fascia as in scraping to the quantity of a fingernail or an inch inside; then pierce the fascia until the space comes near the vein, and that is the level of the water, then draw it forth, and throw away this instrument because that is its form.
