de plusors enfans	of many children

de l’enfant mort	of the dead child

Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if he falls on his feet, it is a light attraction, and the remedies at the mouth of the marrow are light.

Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose womb an infant had died in, then she conceived another on top of that, and rejected the dead one.

je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the cure, and I thought for a long time, and could not soothe the wound.

I touched the wound, and I felt with my hands, until the woman was in a better state; and I watched over the woman for a long time afterwards, and sucked up a little of the swelling from her body; and I did not recall this chapter further than that, because when the masters find an extraordinary thing, they know how to put it right.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the thigh to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Hereafter comes the form of the presser, to which one adds the books; and at .ij. turnings as .ij. heads of the ligaments.

Here is the translation:

These instruments are all superior, and are multiplied in their similarities; and when the mirrors have appeared to them, so much is hastier the work, and higher at home according to their quantity.

Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the secondary inflammation hurries.

And if the mouth of the womb is constricted, we have said the treatment of sternutum, and fumigation with herbs; and if it does not respond to all that we have said, beware lest you do not fall into the trap; but it is fitting that what is at the mouth of the womb, you tie to the thigh of the woman, then anoint with ointment tetrafarmaçon; if it will settle and stay, it will come forth; but however, when it settles thus, a bad odor comes from the stomach and head, and harms the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Here is the translation:

de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have a perceived foundation, thus it is stopped up subtly: so it is necessary then to apply the poultice that perceives it thus to its finger, and does not perceive it with spatula agut, and gathers the laying that it does not touch; then put on a moillie lane in wine and oil, then the treatment of ointment until it is healthy.

de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from its foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Here is the translation:
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that penetrate just to the bladder, and just to the middle of the rod, and they reach just to the joint of the thigh, and just to the top of the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one recognizes the persistent fistula in the foundation, and does not miss it: and it is that you put your right index finger on the foundation, and put a subtle needle of copper or iron in the fistula when there is no twistedness.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is twistedness, you put a subtle probe of lead, or horsehair, until you feel the probe or hair on your finger; and if you do not feel it, and it does not come from pertussive egestion nor ventosity nor ver, as we have said: know that it does not pierce at all; so hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is piercing just next to the bladder or next to the urinary duct, if the urine jumps out, and cannot be stopped by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced just to the joint of the thigh, then the probe comes just to the place; if there is no twistedness and the invention of the pain therein, then it is that it is already bowed, and no medicine nor sudden remedy by ointment; and in these persistent fistulas there is no cure except through labor, and vanity of the foolish doctors who intervene.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In one who is not entirely perspired and is not entirely ancient, there is hope of health through fire, as I have experienced it, and it is that the patient places himself between your hands on his back; and lift his legs up to his knees, and bend his knees towards his belly; then apply a gentle touch of iron, or of lead if there is tortuosity, until you know where the tenderness comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it in the depths, then you must put your index finger there, and soon you will feel that the tenderness has been perceived; and discover where you feel between your fingers the skin or flesh, then know that it is perspired; if you don't work on it, one cannot heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One can barely heal any of them, but it happens rarely; and the aid that one makes, if it is to heat the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as it was said before; and apply it all hot in the fistula, until it reaches deep into the depths; and do this two or three times, until you know that these worn-out skin folds are dry, which resemble a bird's feather; and then treat the wet tenderness with poultice, until that skin is dry, then treat with ointment, softening and soothing the skin.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healthy, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If he is thus, it cannot be healthy; and if you hold between, and do not perceive just to the finger which is at the bottom, and between your finger and the hold a thick covering of flesh or skin, and you see the fistula that shows the covering of the vein; if you cut from the beginning of the fistula, and apply beforehand the hold, and then the cautery afterwards, until it reaches the head of the hold; and the hold will be delivered, and will fall; then remove those decayed flesh that seem like a bird's feather, and none will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood does not come to you, and it is short between you and the vein, then cauterize with fire or with medicinal water.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For fire cauteries assemble two things: it is to know, the art of combining those decayed flesh, and the drying of blood and the purging of moisture; then the treatment of wet wounds in mud or in crushed coal, until the limbs open widely, and the decayed flesh opens into the wound; then treat the wound of festering ulcers by applying dry medicine, and these are the dried medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, then it is healthy and does not relapse again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes near the deep foundation, and is separated from the body, then you should apply your finger or foundation, and inquire about that.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	Here is the translation:
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes they are fistulas in this manner: and it is when you push the tent into the fistula, and it is on the side where the foundation of the skin is above the leather, if you take a tender point at the top according to this form.
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And thrust it deep into the fistula until it reaches the head, and thrust the tent entirely along the thread in the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pierced in the margin of the foundation within, then extract the thread of that perforation, so that you push your finger or foundation; and draw out the head of the thread, and join the two heads together, and hold one to the other, and let it be for a day or two; and restrain it sometimes, until the threads grasp those things that are between them, and cicatrize; then cure the wound until it is soldered and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pass, if you make it pass in all the ways that you can, so it is not too deep inside.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not seem to make a copper plate for the ulcer's dressing, and then the treatment, as we have said, until it is healthy.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spiny spatula with which one makes the fistula is very awkward on one side and cutting; and on the other side not, because one does not grasp what one should not grasp, as you see here.
des emorroydes	of the emproys (possibly a medieval term for a type of medical instrument or procedure)
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Here is the translation:
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Here is the translation:
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the dryness of the veins or base
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is dryness of feces in the intestine, and by constraint of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to reset a dislocated finger or toe, which does not allow it to become moist; then treat it until it becomes stable if it is necessary; and if it cannot be stabilized, then restart the treatment more forcefully than before, until it heals much, and is scarred; then treat it until it is healthy.
dou fremit	you excrete
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Gangrene is a small, faulty appearance that eats away at the body, and it spreads much in depth; and often one finds the coldness, and feels it as if dead from numbness, and it comes to all of the body, and more in the hands than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the treatment is that you take a thread of an eagle's feather, or a strong vulture's feather, and place that thread on the numbness, so that the circles surround the numbness entirely; then turn your hand around the entire thread, and insert it deeply, and scrape out the numbness from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make a tool in the form of a cane or iron, and be subtle below and draw above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not prick, for you must hold at the finger, and press; And if you see, cauterize the affected area, as it is before or in the chapter of cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of theclyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never make a clyster of silver or copper, or of tin or lead alloy; and never use these small and large instruments, according to those for whom they are prepared.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those that one prepares for the treatment of children who are weak and painful are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large clyster is above, wide, or the belly is tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there is a separation where the intestines are tied, as you see, and the head is perceived within; and have on one of the sides II punctures, and in the other I; and let the intestines be where one puts medicines from a beast's bladder or parchment, and let it be totally surrounded by small punctures, and have between each puncture I thread of space, then put in these punctures I strong twisted thread in X or within, and assemble the intestines as if it were a basket; and when the medicine is inside, if you bind to the instrument before with a strong thread, then tighten; and that's the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine be not too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clistere with oil or egg yolk, or similar thing, then put it lightly; then sprinkle the minister's hands together, so that it is totally visible, then extract the clistere, and lift the patient's legs to the parapet, and if the medicine wants to exit, let it exit as much as it can; and if it sleeps one night entirely, it is a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you treat the patient for a disease of bowel disorder, and the medicine hastens to be absorbed, then recommend it as long as he is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the morrow is at the foundation, or an abscess, it should be the subtlest cluster, as for a child; and that's the subtle form of the cluster on the skin where the skin should be held steady:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken in the division about the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments with hands and medicine, according to the accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the locations where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	Things that wounds are made by are a blow of stone, and a cut of sword and of knife, or of lance or of stick or of arrow, or similar things; or those that are made according to the laws of the body, as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the foot, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, because the remembrance will come into its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, beware if it is from a blow of stone or similar things, and the skin is completely broken and the wound is great, and you doubt the presence of an abscess: if you make it quickly healthier by cephalic means if little blood comes out of the wound, and let the healing be contrary to the injured part; and avoid the patient's repletion with wine and coarse meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to be healthy, if his food is diminished, and he does not drink wine, nor eat meat; and put on the wound, if it becomes apostemed here and there, cotton soaked in rose oil or in wine steeped; and if there is no aposteme there, if put on the wound, so it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by air, powder, which I will say a little about later; and if he has moved his arm, if put on some ointments, until it be healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, such as a sword or similar wound, and the edges cannot be assembled by themselves, then assemble them by suturing, as I will say for wounds of the belly, concerning the stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is uncovered by the bone, and it is shallow, and holds only for a short time, if it suppurates; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse food, like you test and cook thoroughly, as with roasted meat, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find a wound with putrid matter, and it does not adhere to the bone, cut away all the putrid flesh, and pour on water; then cure. And if it has entered into the wound or vein, without delay, and it cannot be staunched by medicines, seek out the artery, and if you find it dislocated, bind it with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and it is that you apply this powder which soothes in this way that the arsenic has not moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the method of the powder is this: take incense, one part; dragon's blood, two parts; living chalk, three parts, and grind it subtly, and apply it to the wound, and hold it firmly in place, until it adheres well and joins with all its sap; then bind it well, and leave it without loosening, so it does not inflame; for one does not stop the medicine until it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And often one makes a poultice of hot ashes when there is no incense nor the blood of dragon, but only that the wound has not been treated.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the arsenic has moved into the wound, similarly in this case, if you do not put this powder; but put on some digestive ointments, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, so that it throws out pus; then treat with other treatments until it is healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the fracture of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then I will teach you subtle pincers; and I will tell you about the breaks of the head afterwards.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes to the neck and it is simple, then there is no difference between this one and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerves, then there is no other engine than to leave the treatment, and not put anything constricting, for it harms the nerves and makes them retract; and do not put on the wound anything cold, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but be the soothing medicine, such as hot water with sweet oil, and mix it with rose oil, and cook it in hot water, and other mine preparations according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, thus lay on bandages, then treat it until it is healthy.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and it is uneven and full of swelling, then pierce or cut below the level; and if the artery is severed, and blood flows out, then cauterize to stop the bleeding, and bind, and apply a ligature; and if the spine of the throat is severed, or the veins, and the conduits are watched, so that the flesh goes, if you cut the vein on the side of the throat, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape; and then hold steady, and leave for some days, then cure with ointments as long as it takes to be healthy; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then dig; and if there are pieces of bone, then remove the broken fragments you can, and those that you cannot have, leave until the wound closes, and is dry and light on the surface; and if the wound is fresh, then sprinkle with the powder that I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has become fistulous, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	from a wound of a lance or a knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a lance or dagger, and the wound is deep, then examine the wound to see if there are any ventosities that the patient does not feel: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh in all its blood, then do not put powder on it at the first hour, nor bind it with a bandage so the blood does not stagnate within, and it returns to the heart, and kills the patient; but apply an attractive ointment, and reapply it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, then put much cotton on the wound to suck out the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more; so there will be no spasms, nor bad tremors of the heart, nor strange movements of the limbs; and when you see good dispositions, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Here is the translation:
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, or on the chest or back, if the treatment of what is in front; if it is large, with stitching; and if it is small, with powder, and if it is pressed into the bone, and in covering pieces, so that the wound heals, and the traits are fresh if they are aligned; and if they are not aligned, then let the wound putrefy, then ease the extractions; and for other wounds on other members, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	Here is the translation:
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The ruptures of the belly are large and medium and small; from a large wound sometimes the intestine is hurt, or the nerves of the intestines, because of their introduction; and the stitching is more painful, and sometimes it is better to have a small wound than a large one, because they put the intestines back in place more easily, if they are not put back in hot water; for when the intestine swells so much that it feels cold, it returns more easily, and thus it is better to have a moderate wound, because they reset the intestine to its place like other II And know that the rupture of the belly is according to IIII manners: the II common stitches happen in the stitching of the belly, and the stitching of other wounds on the body and II other proper stitches are common to other wounds; and anyway they are more proper with the stitching of the belly, and I will say each one and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestine is outside, and a grievous thing is to put it back, this is by one of two manners: either through the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is frozen, warm it up in this manner: moisten a sponge or a cloth with lukewarm water, or you cook in lukewarm water and cypress and spike, and raise the intestine until the swelling is gone; and no time make it restrained again, and it is more dead than alive from being deflated.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if you moisten the intestine with lukewarm water or lotions and evil humors are cooked, for by this the entrance is alleviated a little; and if it cannot enter, make a little opening in the wound to cope with the hemorrhoids; and the first cure is more dead than the incision, that we should not incise without great necessity; and this is the instrument for cutting: if you cut within the curve and do not weaken, and see here the form.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine bursts forth, if you reset it according to its natural form in its proper place, you will have the power to do so, for this is worth much.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the belly, you should make the patient sit on their back, and put their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the upper part of the belly, you should raise the head and chest higher than the lower parts, and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two regions, you should arrange it so that the injured part is higher than the other; and thus you should manage what I say about large and moderate wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, take what you have prepared, then hold it between your hands and minister gently, so that you tighten the entire rupture with your hand, and bring together the lips; and this is the common method of suturing, and it is that you take a needle or several, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave at the head of the wound a space of two fingers, and insert a needle where it has a strong thread; and pierce the two sides of the skin with the two sides of the siphac, which is beneath the skin, as much as you make them pierce from that part, and bring together the two heads of the siphac three times; then tighten with a double thread around the needle of two parts, then bring together the two sides of the wound gradually, and then leave a space of two fingers, and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you did for the first needle, and do not cease from doing so according to what you have need of needles, until the entire wound is restrained; and be moderate needles, between subtle and coarse, for subtle needles take in all the flesh, and too coarse ones cannot enter well: therefore it is necessary that they are moderate; and do not push the needles too far into the flesh and skin, lest they take in and open the wound before the suture; and then cover the heads of the needles, so that they do not bother the patient while sleeping, and put a tent or drapery over the heads of the needles to hold them in place for a long time, and leave them until the wound is sewn; and this method of suturing with needles is more convenient for small wounds, for it suffices to insert one or two second sutures; and when you have pierced these sides three times, then reinsert the needle at the part where you began, in the manner that they sew clothes; and put a space between each suture the width of a small finger; this suturing serves the man, and I treated a wound on a certain person who had a belly wound, which was injured by a knife, and it was more than a palm wide, and it had intestines two palms wide, and it was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I will remove the intestine then when it has been established for 24 hours, and the wound was sewn up to 15 days, and I cured him, and he was healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the doctor who had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not cure him with any ointment, because I was in a place where they didn't find any, nor any medicines; and I put cotton on the wound many times a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healthy.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle, and sew the defective part up to the inner part; when it has pierced the right heart in a straight line, if you have stitched or sewn with the needle, and make it pierce another part of the defective inner part; and the understanding of this stitching is that you stitch just as the pelterer makes the pellets, and that you leave one time the thread of one part, and take it up again from another, until the stitching is entirely complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of cauterization, which Galen described properly, is thus: as if no font, which assemble the two parts naturally, and apply one head to the other head, in such a way: fix a needle or head of a mirror adjacent, and make it pierce the entire limb, and let the two heads of the mirror; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the defective part up to that within, as the two heads of the mirror; then make it pierce one and the other from the defective part up to that within, in the other heads of the mirror that are on the other side; and this is the most common manner of cauterization.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen said this in his speech, and no one bears witness, that one should cauterize the belly with two needles, or it has thread in each; and one should insert one needle on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew wounds; and know that when the rupture is within the belly, it is a more grievous cauterization than on other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound in its entirety, even if the arrow has moved, then reset the intestine, and the gut; then put on a powder made from charcoal, and if the arrow has moved, then put on no ointment that is present, until the wound heals; and cut the thread, and sew the skin, and the membrane; then cure the wound as the others, until it is healthy; and if you have no medicines, then put on, soon as it begins to heal, cotton much, and remove it twice a day until it is healthy.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not have mastery of another medicine in many dispositions where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not make common unity with the principal members, then it is necessary that you apply a light ointment in oil of temperate heat, or in oil of rose, and put it between the angles, and beneath the seats; and if there is pain or porridge in the belly, and often happens, then cleanse with wine vinegar tincture, and similarly if the porridge reaches just to the intestine; and pierce within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called "jeune" cannot heal when it is wounded, and this is because of the delicacy of the veins that are there, and because of the subtlety of the entire body, and the approaching of its natural tendency towards nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the intestine jumps away from the wound, set it back in place like the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has turned towards yellow or black, then you must lay the black area that is being drained of blood, because there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the ligament, and put the two heads hanging from the part below the wound until you feel the extraction when the intestines pull, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the good intestine
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is round, and the wound is small, then one can restore it in some homes, because I saw that a man was wounded or pierced by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and became swollen and turned into a fistula, and hindered digestion and ventilation; I applied treatment according to what I could, and did not cease from subtly treating until he was healthy, and the wounds healed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him sweat, I doubted that the patient did not have a bad thing in his stomach; and there was no harm, but it remained in better dispositions, and they were eating and drinking; and certain experimentors said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it must be tied in such a way: take firm hold of large testes, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the firm hold covers the mouth, put it on both lips, so that it extracts its mouth thus; and then cover the head, and it holds itself so that it cannot dislodge, then put another firm hold afterwards in the same way as before, until the wound is completely closed; and sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the intestine is injured, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a subtle thread that is taken from the intestine of an animal, in such a way: take the head of this intestinal thread which is very delicate, and then tie it to the head of the twisted thread, then put the thread into the needle, and sew up the intestine, and reassemble it in its place; and this manner of sewing with firm hold is not done except according to the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the gut intestines, so there is no remedy unless subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Here is the translation:
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the true nodation that it is hard and white, where one does not feel pain, and it is also like the feather of a bird; and sometimes it appears clear, and sometimes dense; sometimes little, and sometimes enough; and I have already spoken in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healthy, and there is no flesh, it is only by one of the eight causes: it is to know, by the small amount of blood or pus; or through its malice; or because there is hard flesh within, and on the lips, which does not allow flesh to grow; or there is too much swelling; or the skin is porous, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is a kind of pestilence; or because the property of the region is slow digestion, and slow health, and weak by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	or it is necessary that I teach you to know the treatment of fistula which is done by operation of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Here is the translation:
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	Here is the translation:
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or principal member does not grieve you, as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered, and there is decay and blackness, so remove all the decay, then heal the things that are hurt so they may be healthy; and if it is not healthy, and return to the beginning, know that you were not able to be above: uncover and search until you reach the bottom, and remove all the decay, then restore the place; and if it is thus healthy, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If this does not work, know that the decay is too deep, so you cannot reach it; if there is no other remedy than to leave it to nature; and if there is a small rotten bone, and you can remove it with pincers, remove it with an appropriate instrument, and if there are many bones, remove them all, do not leave even one; and if the moisture makes you contrary, and there is no error or fear, then cut and scrape and separate, and deliver the bones.

Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	It was a young man around 30 years old who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, so much that the matter went to the leg and became inflamed with a large abscess, and there was no way to open it; but the doctor foolishly operated on it, and scraped away many matters, and it turned into a fistula, and there were many openings that completely drained the moisture from the body; and many doctors treated him for two years, and there was no wisdom in the art of hands, so much that I was called in, and saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being cured, and what corroded through the openings of the large body; and the body of the young man became red, and had a citrine color.

de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess on the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe. des vils	bad hairs
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres. The treatment with iron is in two manners: one is that they cut, and draw out the black blood; and the other manner is that you open the vein, and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The cutting is according to this manner: first raise the leg with warm water very strongly, so that the gross blood is subtled, then hold the leg of the patient from above the thigh just to the part below the knee; then cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a large cut, then draw out and extract the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the virtue of the patient can suffer; and then bind, and instruct that they abstain from eating black coal; and recommence the evacuation and health when the veins are full, and annoy the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Here is the translation:
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vision is constricted and twisted and entwined together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must bend it straight, but do not cover it; and pull it as we have previously stated.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron that one uses to cover the vision is curved, and does not cut, so it does not cover the vein; and it is of great curvature, for if it were subtle, it would cover the vein, but being large as we have said, and this is the shape.
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is generated in the legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in earth where there is no moisture; and by chance grows elsewhere than in the legs, and this comes from the putrefaction that arises beneath the skin, as it comes within the body of serpents and worms, generating between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And the signs of the beginning of this vein are that a very great inflammation comes in the leg, then the veins change, and the vein starts to issue forth, just like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the chest is open, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of cloth one and a half inches up to two inches, and the knot, and leave the cloth on the leg, and every time it does not stay in place, if you wrap around the cloth, and the knot; and if it is too long, cut off part of it, and wrap the remainder, and do not cut into its root, until it is all issued; for if you cut it, it returns into the flesh, and causes abscesses and putrefaction in the limb, and bad disease; because it is necessary that it be treated little by little up to the head, and nothing remains or festers; and there are often times when this vein is treated with five or ten inches of length, and a few men came to me who had it issuing from ten inches of length, and when you cut it, the reason bursts out or perforates, and pierces deeply, so that everything issues; and let the material that is inside be evacuated, and apply medicines to soothe putrefaction any day, then the cure is like the abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And many times at this vein of the hand, and especially when it opens in the joint of the foot, or of the foot itself, and a lot of pus comes out, and from which it jumps abundantly; cure it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of sores that grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "cattle disease", because it often affects cattle, and is a small sore that grows between skin and flesh, and spreads throughout the body, ascending and descending, and one feels it well from member to member, until it reaches the skin or it falls, and jumps fiercely; and it is caused by the putridity of certain humors, such as worms and serpents and lumbrics and ascarides in the belly; and there is doubt about its malice, for when it spreads through the body, and it rises to the head, and it reaches the eye, by chance returning, and destroys the eye; and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see the patient and treat, if it cannot be cured otherwise: then it is necessary that you place the limb above and below with a strong lien tightly, then cut above and draw out forcefully, and if the vein is deeply embedded in the flesh, and you do not find it, if you cauterize with fire as much as it will die; and the greatest harm it does, is that it corrodes the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the eye, hold the eyebrow firmly, then cut above, and draw out forcefully; and it is necessary to use the patient's mundification of bodily medicines solutives for evil humors porries, and beware of eating bad meat in a putrid manner.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes into some members, and then moves from member to member; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and I examined her arm, and saw a small inflammation in the vein of the arm; and soon after, I saw it swell up like a worm at the shoulder, faster than anything, like living silver when it runs from one place to another; the pain departed from that place, and attached itself to the shoulder, and then soon after spread throughout the entire body, until it reached the other arm; then she told me that it would often return across the body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very surprised how it moved from member to member, for I had never seen this disease in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had seen many who wanted to move the pain from one place to another, but I did not see it, as I saw in the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and uncovered veins, and therefore appeared this constrained ventosity; and it did not appear according to this reason to those who are delicate, and have moist bodies and responsive veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you want to cure this illness, and the patient feels that pain, it appears as we have said, if the lie is above and below hastily, and then cope with it so much that the wind constrains the place; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes, if you treat what drives away the winds, like fetid pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places of the body where they fall.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is that there are those with large points, and small ones, and notched ones, and soldered ones; and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those where there are pieces; and that which falls on no principal member falls in two manners: either on a principal member it notches, like the brain, heart, liver, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When the body falls into a bad state of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you about later, appears: if it happens that you extract this arrow, because death comes afterwards in many ways; and when this bad sign does not appear, and the arrow is not deeply implanted, then pull it out, and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the signs of the brain when the arrowhead is in it and pierces the bone, and the syphilis falls which is on the brain, are scotomia and swelling and inversion and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and perturbation of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps it loses force from the nostrils, or the ears; and perhaps it loses speech and voice; and falls into a white moist wound resembling a pustule, and falls also like a broken char; and if this sign appears, then hold back from the cure, and pull out the arrowhead if it is not in.
