And when it is completely dislocated, one must make the patient sit upright, and hold the administration strongly by the leg, above the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left hand twice, then extend it high, and firmly set the foot high; and do this twice, as we have said, in setting and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, start the work again, for it will return; and if it cannot return thus, make the patient sit on his back on the ground, and firmly fix the foot on the ground between his thighs, and tie the bandages around, so the patient does not move; then hold the administration with one hand, and another administration extends the foot with their hands or with a strap, so it is against the collar of the foot; then extend each administration equally, and the foot is held firmly between the thighs of the patient to retain the patient when they are extended; then put the mirrors equally to set the dislocation with their hands, and another administration holds the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it has reached the point, set the plaster and poultices on top, and bind firmly, and apply a bandage to the leg, and wrap the veins that are on the back of the knee, so the ligatures are not too tight; then let it be for two or three days, and if the ligatures soften, bind again; then remove it on the third or fourth day, and delay going to see the patient for four days; and if it goes beyond this term, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses arise from it, it is necessary that you treat them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healthy.
des dois	of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the fingers are dislocated, it is necessary to extend them gently without force, and this is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any of the two toes or feet, it is necessary that you make the patient sit on a flat surface or table, straight and upright, and put your foot on what opens from these joints, then press your foot firmly until it returns to its place; and when it is even, and there is no gap, set under the sole of the foot a small table at two inches, then bind firmly, and let it be for three days, then remove it; and make them rest, until they are healthy.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and one wants to restore it, many times the patient dies: if you are not presumptuous in the cure, be wise in the art and have long experience, and be pitiful and merciful and tardy, not hard; and use gentle remedies at the beginning of soothing abscesses hotly, and leave the patient in God's hands, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place, so that the abscesses may not come back to life; and when the limb is in its place, then administer gentle remedies soothing abscesses hotly, and cure the wound, as it is fitting, with desiccated ointments; and if with dislocation there is a fracture, and you do not find the bone, set them, and do what we have said in simple illnesses; and beware of entering into fear's path, according to what I have said, for it is worth nothing according to your Creator, and for the salvation of your arm and body.
Amen	Where fire cautery is commanded for the patient to let the hairs grow as long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
